CHAPTER IX

┼ЪR─АDDIA

This subject is of groat practical importance from several points of viow.

The Brahmapur─Бpa definos ┼Ыr─Бddha as follows. whatever is giron with faith to br─Бlmanag intending it to be for the (banofit of) trs at a proper time, in a proper place, to desery ing porsong and in accordance with the prescribed procedure is called sraddha 7st, The Mit on Y─Бj I 217 defines sraddha As ‘abandonment with faith of an article of food or some sub stituto thoroof, intending it for (the benefit of) the departed’. Tho Kalpataru on sr─Бddha defined it as ’the giving up of sacri ficial material intending it for pitrs and its acceptance by br─Бhmanas’. The Sraddhaviveka of Rudradhara and the Srad dhaprak─Б┼Ыa dofine ┼Ыr─Бddba in the same way as the Mit, but in a more inrolved manner, Yaj. I. 268 (= Agnipurana 163. 40-41) states that the pntrs via. Vasus, Rudras and Adityas that are the deities of ┼Ыr─Бddha, being gratified by gr─Бddha, give gratification to tlio ancestors of human beings. viz, the father, paternal grand-father and the paternal great. grand-father are respectively to be identified with the three orders of superintending pitr deities, vix. Vasus, Rudras and Adityas, when performing ┼Ыr─Бddha. A.ccording to some,752 sraddha denotes three things, viz, hama, the offering of pinda (ball of cooked food) and gratification of br─Бbmapas invited to a dinner; the application of this word to any one of these three can only be in a secondary sense.

A firm believer in the doctrine of kar ma, punarjanma (re incarnation) and karma-up─Бka (explained above) may find it difficult to reconcile that doctrine with the belief that by offer ing balls of rice to his three deceased paternal ancestors a man brings gratification to the souls of the latter. According to the doctring of punarganma (as Fery clearly and succinctly put in Br. Up IV. 4.4 and Bhagavad-git─Б 2 22 ) 753 the spirit leaving one body enters into another and a new one. But the doctrine of offering balls of rice to three ancestors requires that the spirits of the three ancestors even after the lapse of 50 or 100 years are still capable of enjoying in an ethereal body the flavour or essence of the rios balls wafted by the wind. Further, Yaj. I 269 (which is the same as M─Бrk, 29, 38, Matsya-purana 19.11-12, Agnipur─Бna 163, 41-42) provides that the grand fathers (i. e, pitrs) being themselves gratified (by the offerings of food in ┼Ыr─Бddha) bestow on men (their descendants) Jong life, progeny, wealth, learning, heaven, molс╣гa (final beatitude), all happiness and kingdom. In the Matsya-purana (chap. 19, Verse 2) a question is asked by the sages how food which a br─Бhmana (invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha) eats or which is offered into fire is enjoyed by departed spirits that might have assumed (after death) good or evil forras of bodies. The answer given (verses 3-9) is that fathers, grand-fathers and great-grand fathers are identified with Vagus, Rudras and Adityas regpectively according to Vedic passages, that the name and gotra (mentioned at the time of ┼Ыr─Бddha), the mantras uttered and faith carry to the patts the offerings made, that if one’s

IV)

Does sraddha serve no purpose

337

to perform it or is it because ┼Ыr─Бddha produces no consequences or is it that it is not proved that putrs and the rest are gratified by ┼Ыr─Бddha? To the first he replies that there are such passages as ’therefore & wise mad must perform sr─Бddha with all his efforts that lay down the obligation; nor is the 2nd objection proper, since Y─Бj. I. 269 does declare the rewards ( of gr─Бddha ) viz, long life &o. Nor is the third alternative acceptable. In the ┼Ыr─Бddha rites it is not that the mere ancestors named Deva datta and the like are the recipients and that they are denoted by the words pitr, pit─Бnaha and prapit─Бmaha, but that those vords denote them as accompanied by the superintending deities FIZ. Vasus, Rudras and Adityas. Just as by the words Deva datta and the like what is denoted is not merely the bodies (so named) nor merely the souls, but what is denoted by the words is individual souls as particularised by the bodies; in the same way the words pitt and the like denote Devadatta and others together with the superintending deities (viz. Vasus, Rudras and Adityas). Therefore, the superintending deities viz, the Vasus and the rest, being gratified by the food and drink offered by the sons and the rest, gratify those also viz. Dersdatta and the rest and endow the performers (of ┼Ыr─Бddha) with such towards as male progeny and the rest. Just as a woman expecting to be a mother becomes gratified by partaking of the food and drink for which she has a longing in pregnancy and which is given to her by another person for the sustenance of the child in the womb, she satiates also the child in her womb and endows those that offer her the food and drink for which she has longings by bestowing on them some reward in return. Thus the pitts denoted by the words father, granda father and great-grand-father are the deities Vagus, Rudras and ─Аdityas, and not merely (human beings called ) Devadatta and the rest. Hence these deities of ┼Ыr─Бddba become the recipients (of gifts) in the ┼Ыr─Бddha rite, are gratified by the ┼Ыr─Бddha and gratify in their turn the ancestors of human beings. Theory of ┼Ъr─Бddha examined

any thing on their progeny. It appears very probable that the Worship of ancestors by means of ┼Ыr─Бddhas was a very ancient institution and that the doctrines of Punarjanma and Farmauip─Бka were comparatively later ones and that Hinduisme being all-embracing retained the institution of ┼Ыr─Бddhas while adopting also the doctrine of metempsychosis. The institution ef sraddha is from one point of view an excellent one. It provides an occasion for remembrance of one’s ancestors and relatives that were dear and near then living The ─Аryasamaja objects to the institution of ┼Ыr─Бddha and interprets pitrs in the Rgreda as meaning living men in the T─Бnaprastha stage. It may be noted that the texts support both views. The Sat, Br, expressly says that food is offered to the father of the sacrificer in the words ’this is for thee,’ Vispu Dh. S. 75, 4 ‘He whose father is dead may put down a pinda for his father &c,’ On the other hand Manu I 284 states that fathers are spoken of as Yasus, grandfathers as Rudras &c and Yaj. I. 269 provides that Yasus, Rudras and Adityas are the pitts and the derat─Бs of saddha. These latter are to be explained as con faining an injunction to contemplate upon the pitys as Vasus, Rudras &c.

As stated below (p. 347) with regard to the Rgvedic passages, it Tas on account of the supposed poter of pitrs to benefit or harn the living that the cult of the dead became a prominent feature in primitive societies. Offerings and ceremonies which may hare in most ancient times been prompted in part at least by the desire to placate the ancestors are continued as tokens of pare affection and remembrance. Various beliefs about pitс╣Ыs are mentioned 75% in post-Vedic Literature, The Baud. Dh, S. II. 8. 14 summarizes a brahmana text stating that pits move about in the form of birds, The Au┼Ыanasa-smrti and Devala quoted by the Kalpataru say the same thing. In the V─Бyu par─Бns 759 it is stated that at the time of st─Бddha the ancestors

The Brahmapur─Бna 761 states that sr─Бddha is to be treated of under five hoads, viz, how, where, when, by whom and with what materials, But before proceeding to deal with these five hoads, it is necessary to dilate upon the underlying ideas and significance of the word ‘mtarah’ from the most ancient times of which we have literary records,

The word ‘potr’ means ‘father’, but the word ‘pitarah’ is used in two senses, viz. (1) a man’s three immediate decessed ancestors, (2) the early or ancient ancestors of the human race that were supposed to inbabit a separate world (loka) by them

I Vol. particularly of Yaina (Rg VII. 76. 4, X. 14 10, X, 15. 8-10) 766 The pitts are said to be fond of Soma drink (Rg. X. 15.1 and 5, IX. 97 39), they lie down on ku┼Ыa grass (Rg X15,5), they come with Agni and Indra to partake of the offerings (Rg X, 15. 10 and X, 16.12 ) and Agni is also said to carry the offerings to the prirs (Rg X, 15. 12). Fire is supposed to take the spirit of a crematod person to the prirs (Rg. X 16, 1-2, 5=., V. 18. 2. 10, Rg X. 17, 3). In later works also (e. g. in M─Бrk, chap. 45), Brahm─Б is supposed to have created in the beginning four classes viz. gods, asuras, pitrs and human beings Vide also Brahm─Бndapur─Бna, Prakriy─Б, chap. 8, and upodgh─Бta chap. 9. 35 (ityete pitaro dey─Б dev─Б┼Ыca pitaraс╕е punah anyonyapitaro hyete).

It was supposed that the departed spirit, after the cremation of the body, was endowed with an ethereal body and became associated with Yama, the gatherer of departed men (Rg. X. 14. 1 and 8, X. 15, 14, X 16 5), and with pitrs, The departed spirit went to the world of the patrs and Agni was implored to take the spirit to the world of the departed whose deeds were good and to the stride of Vispu (Rg. X. 14. 9, X, 15. 3, X. 16.4).

343 IV)

The World of Pitts it is said that the pitrs dwell in the third world from this. This means that after bhuloka and antariksa comes the pitriola. In the Br. Up. I 5.16 three wor]ds of men, pitrs and gods are separately mentioned. In Rg. X. 135, 1-7, Yama is spoken of in somewhat different language. He is in this bymn men tioned as a god by himself and not as the first mortal who made a path (Rg. X. 14. 2) or as the gatherer of men (X 14, 1) or as being in company of the pitrs In a few other places Yama is no doubt called r─Бjan and praised in the same breath with Varuna (Rg, X. 14. 7). But such a position is very rarely mentioned, For the further development of Yama and his assistants as the punishers of men for evil deeds, vide pp. 159-160 above and notes 381-386.

There is another division of pitrs viz. Pi┼Вarah somavantah,771 pitarah barhzс╣гadah, pitarah agnisv─Бtt─Бh The latter two are named in Rg X 15 4 and 11 (which occur also in Tai. S. IL 6. 12. 2). The Sat. Br. defines these as follows.-" those that performed a soma sacrifice are putarah somavantah; those that offered cooked oblations (like caru and purod─Б┼Ыa) and secured a world are pitarah barhiс╣гadah; those that did none of these (two actions) and whom fire consumes when burning them are ‘pitarah agnisv─Бtt─Бh;’ these are the only ones that are putarah."

The Tai.772 Br, has & somewhat similar passage and the Kathaka Sambita IX. 6. 17 also refers to these three kinds of pitrs, Later writers introduced certain changes in the mean ings of the words for the different classes of pit?s and also in creased the number of the classes of piirs. For example, the Nandipur─Бna g. by Hem─Бdri states: the petrs of br─Бbmapas are called ‘agnisv─Бtta’, those of ksatriyas ‘barhisadah’, those of vaisyas ‘kavyas’, those of ┼Ы┼лdras ‘auk─Бlin’ and those of mle cobas and untouchables are called ‘vy─Бma’. 773 Even Manu

(pa├▒cajad─Б mama hotram juс╣гadhyam) and other passages, the Ait. Br. (13.7 or 3.31) explains that they are the five classes, viz. Gandharyas rith Apsarases, pitrs, deyas, sarpas and r─Бkszsas, The Nirukta III. S partly follows this explanation and also gives another. In the Atharvayeda X 6. 32 the gods, pitts and men are mentioned in that order. The ancient Vedic tests and practice make a sharp distinction between the Gods and the Pitrs. The Tai.S. VI. 1. 1. 1 states: ’the gods and men divided the quarters, the gods took the east, pitys the south, men the west and Rudras the north. The general rule is that sacrifices for gods are begun in the forenoon, while the pitr-yaj├▒a is performed in the afternoon (San Br.).775 The Sat Br. II. 4.2.2 Darrates that the pitrs wearing the sacred thread over the right shoulder (30d under the left arm) and bending their left knee approached Praj─Бpati, when Prajapati said to them you will hare food at the end of each month (on the Am─Бv─Бsy─Б), your stadh┼л (cordial) will be swiftness of thought and the moon will be your light,’ while to the gods he had said that sacrifice will ba their food and the sun their light. The Tai. Br. 776 I. 3. 10.4 appears to make a distinction between pitrs who are of the nature and position of gods and pit╚Ъs that are more or less like human beings.

The Kau┼Ыika-s┼лtra (1. 9-23) neatly collects in one place the difference in the procedure of the rites meant for gods and for pitс╣Ыs. The performer of rites for gods wears the sacred thread on the left shoulder and under the right armpit, while in the case of the rites for pitrs it is worn on the right shoulder and under the left arm; the rite for gods is either begun facing the east or north, while that for the pitс╣Ыs is begun facing the south; the rite for gods is finished in the north-east (or north or east), while that for the pitrs is completed in the south-west; an action is done only once for pit─лs, while for gods at least thrice or as many times as the texts direct; in going round (parambulating) the right side is turned towards gods and the left one in the case of piс╣гs; offerings are made to gods with the words ‘sv─Бha’ and yaset’, while they are made to pitfs with ‘stadh─Б’ and

In the post-Vedic Literature, particularly in the Puranas, a great deal is said about the origin and classes of pitrs. For example, the V─Бyupur─Бda 56. 18 speaks of three classes of pitrs V─▒z k─Бvy─Бh, barhisadah and agnisv─Бtt─Бh’, while the same Purana, chap. 73, Var─Бha 13. 16 ff, Padma (Srsti 9. 2-4) and Brabmanda IL, 101 speak of the origin of pitrs of seven classes that dwell in heaven, four of which have a forni (m┼лrizmat) and three of which are without form (am┼лrla). The Sat─Бtapa-smrti (6.5-6) speaks of 12 pitra viz. pjodabh─Бjah, lepabh─Бjah, n─Бndimukh─Бh and a┼Ыrumukh─Бh. All such descrip tions have to be passed over from considerations of space.

IV

Promulgators of br─Бddha rites

349

From the sutra period (about 600 B. C) to the most modern among medieval Dharma┼Ы─Бstra works the authors wax eloquent over the praiges or the importance or benefits of the institution of ┼Ыr─Бddhas. One of the earliest works among these, viz. the ─Аp. Dh. S gives the following interesting information : 783 “Forinerly men and gods lived togetlier in this world. The gods went to heaven owing to sacrifices (i. e, as a reward of sacrifices that they performed), but men remained behind, Those among men who perform sacrifices in the same way as the gods did, dwell in the other world (i. e. heaven) with the gods and Brahman. Then (seeing that men lagged behind) Madu promulgated the rite which is designated by the word ‘sraddha’ and which tends to the salvation (or happiness) of mankind. In this rite the Manes (prtarah) are the deities but the br─Бhmadas (that are fed) are in the place of the ─Бhavaniya fire (in which in sacrifices to gods oblations are offered)”. On account of this last s┼лtra Haradatta (com, of ─Аp. Dh, S.) and others hold that feeding the br─Бhmadas is the princi pal act at a ┼Ыr─Бddha. The Brahm─Бndapur─Бpa (Upodgh─Бtap─Бda 9, 15. and 10. 99) speaks of Manu as the promulgator of ┼Ыr─Бddha rites and Viс╣гс╣Зupur─Бpa IIL 1 30, V─Бyu 44, 38 and Bhagavata II, 1, 2% designate Manu as Sraddha-deva. Similarly, in the Santiparva 345.784 14-21 and the Viс╣гс╣Зu-dharmottara L139 14-16 it is stated that the institution of ┼Ыr─Бddha was established in the Boar incarnation by Viс╣гс╣Зu and that Viс╣гс╣Зu should be regarded as dwelling in the three pindas offered to the father, grand-father and great-grandfather From this and from the passage of the ─Аp. Dh. S cited above we may infer that it was believed even several centuries before Christ that the institution of ┼Ыr─Бddhas had a hoary antiquity behind it and that it was as old as Madu, the father of mankind according to the Rgveda (VIII, 63,1, VIII 30. 3.). It is, however, very remarkable that the word *┼Ыr─Бddha’ itself does not occur in any undoubtedly authentic and ancient Vedic passage, though the rite called Pindapitr yaj├▒a 785 (performed on the am─Бv─Бsy─Б of each month by an

The word ┼Ыr─Бddha occurs in the Kathopanisad (1.3.17) ‘whoever proclaims this highly esoteric doctrine in an assembly of br─Бhmadas or at the time of ┼Ыr─Бddha tends to secure immortality.‘786 The other early occurrences of the word ┼Ыr─Бddha known to me are confined to the s─Бtra literature. The most reasonable and probable inference to be drawn from these facts is this that only a few rites (mentioned just above) were known as related to the pritrs and that there fore no need arose for a generic term in very ancient times to comprehend several rites for the pitrs. It is necessary to say a few words about the derivation of the word ‘┼Ыr─Бddha’. That the word is derived from ‘┼Ыraddha’ is quite clear. In the definition quoted above from the Brahma purada and the definition 792 given by Marici and B╚Щhaspati the connection of ┼Ыr─Бddba with ┼Ыraddb─Б is emphasized. The procedure of Astak─Б comprises three parts, riz, homa, inviting br─Бhmadas for dinner (up to seeing them go array after dinner) and the rite called Alyastakya or Anpastak─Б When the Astak─Бs were deemed to be three or four performed in the several months noted above, all these were gone through at each ├Еstaka When the Astak─Б rite vas performed only in one month i. e, after the Full moon in M─Бgha, the above parts were performed on three days, 7th, 8th and 9th of the dark balf. When compressed in one day only, they must have been per formed one after another on the same day.

The Pinda-pitryaj├▒a could be offered on anl─Бv─Бsy─Б only by one who was ─Бhit─Бgni (i. e. had kept the sacred vedic fires). It is impossible to believe that everyone became ─Бhit─Бgai. The case was probably the reverse i, e. only a few became ─Бhit─Бgnis and the rest had only the grbya fira or many of the rest were without even the grhya fire. It appears possible that all were required to offer ┼Ыr─Бddha on am─Бt─Бsy─Б on the analogy of pindapitryajia. As the latter became rare, the requirement of offering sr─Бddha on am─Бvagy─Б remained and in the g┼лtras and smrtis all the details were mentioned under m─Бsi┼Ыr─Бddha and in the case of the other fr─Бddhas the s┼лtras and smrtis pointed out only what was to bs omitted. Hir. Gr. . 13, 3. (edited by Kirste) the name appears to be Madhy─Бvarsa 825 and it is provided that meat is obligatory in it, but that if meat cannot be had then vegetables may be offered. In P─Бr. 826 Gr. (II. 3) the name (as printed) is madhy─Бvarsa which is said to be a 4th Astak─Б in wbich only vegetables are offered. Apararka (p. 422) also appears to call the rite ‘madhya varsa. In the Bhaviс╣гyapur─Бna 877 (Brahma-parya), chap. 183, 4 also this rite is referred to but it is said that therein meat is to be offered. It appears probable that this ancient rite on the 13th of the dark half of Bhadrapads is a precursor of the Mah─Бlaya┼Ыraddha of later times,

If Asyal─Бyana’s view, viz, that there are four Astak─Бs in Hemanta and st┼Ыira, were followed and if the Maghyavarsa ┼Ыr─Бddha were to be performed on the 8th of the dark half of Bhadrapada as N─Бr─Бyana holds, then there would be five Astak─Бs in all. Bhattoji in his Caturpimsatimatagangraha says so.823

Considerations of space forbid the comparison of the above procedure from Ap. Gr. and ─А┼ЫY, Gr. with the procedure described in the other Grhyas┼лtras. It should be noted that several of the s┼лtras often employ the same mantras in the various stages of the rite (as pointed out above in notes 813-814).

It must be said that the Astak─Б ┼Ыr─Бddhas gradually fell into oblivion and are not performed now.

adequate and thorough treatment of all this vast mass would fill a separate volume, but considerations of space forbid such an attempt here. All that can be attempted here at the most (and that too not in all cases) is to present matters chronologi cally i. e, describe how ┼Ыr─Бddha was dealt with in the Saс╣Бhit─Бs and Br─Бhmana texts, then in the comparatively older Gshya and Dharma s┼лtras, then in such early startis as those of Manu and Y─Бj., then in some representative Puradas, then in the early commentaries of Medh─Бtithi, Vij├▒─Бne┼Ыvara and Apar─Бrka, and then in the medieval digests. Even in this way only a skeleton of the ceremonies described in some representative work of each class can be exhibited. Many differences of detail which arose owing to lapse of time, the locality, the sakha and usages of each writer, his individual inclination and his ability, will have to be passed over altogether. In the days of the Pur─Бpas the differences in detail in the several ┼Ы─Бkh─Бs have been adverted to.829a Apart from the smrtis and passages of the Mah─Бbh─Бrata (such as Anu┼Ы─Бsana chap. 87-92) and com montaries on the S┼лtras, on Manu, Y─Бj. and other smptis, the digests on ┼Ыr─Бddha are legion, Only the following digests (arranged in chronological order) have been laid under contri bution in this volume: Kalpataru on ┼Ыr─Бddha; the H─Бralat─Б and Pitrdayit─Б of Aniruddha; the Smrtyarthas─Бra; the Smrticandrik─Б; the Caturvargacint─Бmani (section on ┼Ыr─Бddha) of em─Бdri (which in the B. I, edition covers 1716 pages); the Sr─Бddhaviveka of Rudradhara; the Madanap─Бrij─Бta ; the Sr─Бddhas─Бra (a part of Nrsimhapras─Бda); ┼Ъr─Бddhakriya-kaumudi of Govind─Б.Danda; the Sr─Бddhatattva of Raghunandana ; the ┼Ъr─Бddhagaukhya (part of Todar─Бnanda); the Sr─Бddhakalpalat─Б of Vinayaka alias Nandapandita; the Nirpayasindhu; the ┼Ъz─Бddhamay┼лkha of Nilakantha; the ┼Ъr─Бddhaprak─Б┼Ыa (part of Viramitrodaya); the ┼Ъr─Бddhacandrik─Б of Div─Бkarabhatta ; the Smrtimukt─Бphala (on ┼Ыr─Бddha); the Dharmasindhu; the B─Бlambhatti, a commentary on the Mit─Бksar─Б, While presenting this exhaustive and hetero. geneous material, some generalisations, when called for, will be made here and there. We should now turn to the several matters relating to ┼Ыr─Бddhas,

First comes the question as to who are entitled to offer ┼Ыr─Бddha (┼Ыr─Бddh─Бdhikarin) This matter has been already dealt with in the E, of Dh, vol. IIL Y 739 ff., and on page 763 and od pp. 256-261 (notes 581-588) above. It would be noticed that some (like the Viс╣гс╣Зudharmas┼лtra ) prescribe that whoever takes the wealth of the deceased should of─лer prindas (i, e. per form sraddha for him), while others said that whoever was preferable as entitled to offer pindas to the deceased propositus was to take the wealth. A few matters not mentioned there may be added here. In the Santiparva 65, 13-21 it is narrated83a that emperor M─Бndhat was told by Indra bow Yaradas, Kiratas and similar non-Aryan peoples (that are styled Dasyus in the Epic) are to be made to conduct themselves and it is stated that all dasyus may perform Pitryaj├▒as (in which they should feed men of their own kind and make monetary gifts to them) aod offer money to br─Бhmanas also, The V─Бyupor─Бda (83. 112) also speaks of the Mlecchas as persons that offer oblations to Pitys. The general rule is stated by the Gobhila smrti 61 that the husband should not offer pipda to his wife even if she dies sonless, nor a father to his son por an elder brother to a younger brother. The moral of the story of Nini trho performed ┼Ыr─Бddha for his predeceased son and repented for having done so as it was dharmasankara is the same, Vide Anu┼Ы─Бsanaparra 91, Apararka (p. 538) quotes a verse from ┼Юaс╣нtrim├│┼Ыan-mata that a father should not perform the ┼Ыr─Бddha of his son Ror an elder brother of a younger one, But Brhat par─Б┼Ыara (p. 153) appears to state that even this general rule may have to be set aside sometimes. It is emphas ized 832 that he alone deserves to be called putra, who, while the father is alive, obeys his words, and gives plenty of food (to br─Бhmanas) every year (after his father’s death) and who offers pindas (to his ancestors) at Gay─Б. The general rule laid down was that a child, whose upanayana has not been performed, is like a ┼Ы┼лdra and lacks authority to utter Vedic passages (vide Ap. Dr. S. II, 6, 15. 19, Gaut. II, 4-5, Vas. II 6, Visou Dh. Medh─Бtithi on Manu L 172 explains that a minor son, even though not initiated into Vedic study by upanayana, can offer water to his father, perform the nava┼Ыr─Бddhas (mentioned above in n. 593) and repeat such mantras as “Sundhant─Бm pitaraс╕е’ required in these rites, but since he has no srauta or grluya fire of his own he can not per form such ┼Ыr─Бddhas as the p─Бrvana. Therefore when Manu (IX. 106 ) says that by the birth of a son a man discharges his dobt to his progenitors the Diyabh─Бga (XI, 34) explains that the word putra stands for the three descendants up to the great grandson, since all the thrbe are entitled to perform the p─Бr vapa-┼Ыr─Бddha and equally benefit the ancestors by the pindas they offer, and that the word putra is not to be taken literally but only as illustrative in order to include the great-grandson, since one may with difficulty find & text expressly mentioning tho adl─▒k┼лra of the grandson (as a performer of gr─Бddha and taker of wealth) but there is no text expressly mentioning the great-grandson separately (as the taker of wealth and giver of pinda) 836 On Y─Бj. . 50 which lays down that when the father dies or has gone to a distant country or is overwhelmed by calamities (incurable diseases or the like) bis debts should be paid by the sons or grandsons, the Mit, adds that even when a son or grandson receives no ancestral property the father’s debts must be paid, the only difference being that the son has to pay the principal as well as the interest, while the grandson

IV 1

Meaning of ‘putra’

has to return only the principal and has to pay no interest and the Mit. quotes & Terge of Brhaspati 87 where all the three descendants are mentioned in one breath and the Mit, adds that the great-grandson has not to pay even the principal if he has received no ancestral property. This last remark implies that tho Mit. regarded that the great-grandson was also included in the extended sense of ‘putra’. Y─Бj. I, 51 begins by saying that whoever takes the wealth of a deceased person has to pay the latter’s debts, so the great-grandson would have to pay the great-grand-father’s debts if he received the agsets of the grand-father. Therefore the Mit, on II, 50 expressly mentions that a great-grandson need not pay his great-grand-father’s debts if he received no assets, because, otherwise being included in the extended meaning of putra, he would have had to pay. There was no necessity to bring in or mention the prapautra under II, 50 if the Mit, did not include the prapautra in the word putra. Again on Y─Бj. II, 51 (‘putrahinasya rikthinah’) the Mit. included even prapautra under the word pittra. This shows that the Mit. is quite conscious that the three descendants of a man form one group and succeed to his estate and liabilities and putra includes three descendants wherever the context so requires. If the word ‘putra’ is not to be taken as only illustrative and as including both grandson and great-grandson, s├йrious difficulties will arise even in the interpretation of Yaj. on which the Mit. comments. For example, in Y─Бj. II. 135-136 it is said that when a gonless man dies his wife, daughters and other heirs (named there ) succeed one after another. If ‘putra’ is taken to mean only ‘son’ and no one else, then on the death of a man without a son his wife or daughter (whoever is alive) will take the wealth oven if a son’s son exists. But that would be absurd and is not stated by any one. Therefore the word putra has to be interpreted in a wider sense in a proper context. Many works such as the Vyavah─Бramay┼лkha, the Viramitrodaya, the Dattakamim─Бns─Б interpret the word ‘putra’ as including three generations. Therefore, though the Mit, in its remarks on inheritance and succession expressly names the son and grand

IVI

Times for sraddhas

Just as the king is an ultimate heir and also the guardian of all minors, 80 he is like the son of a person (who has no relatives left) for performing sraddhas

The nest question is about the times when sraddha is to be performed. It has been seen above (vide H. of Dh. Yol, IT. P. 696 ff) that long before the time of the Sat. Br. five daily observances (called Mah─Бyaj├▒as) were prescribed for each house-bolder, viz the sacrifice to beings, that to men, that to the Fathers, that to the gods and that to Veda

The Sat. Br. and the Tai, ─Б, (I. 10) say further that this daily rite in which one offers suadh─Б (food) to the Fathers even up to water was called pitryaisia. Manu III. 70 defines Pitryaj├▒a as tarpana (satiating ancestors with the offerings of water). Manu II, 82 provides that an householder, should daily perform a ┼Ыr─Бddha with food or with water or with milk, roots and fruits and thus please the Fathers. Sraddha originally meant & sacrifice performed for the Fathers on Am─Бr─Бsy─Б (vide Gaut, 15. 1-2 ).838a By applying that word to the daily offering of water to the Manes what is intended to be conveyed is that the special characteristics of ┼Ыr─Бddha in the strict sense are to be extended to this daily rite so far as possible. Am─Бv─Бsy─Б is of two kinds, Siniv─Бli and Kuh┼л, Those who keep ┼Ыrauta fires should perform ┼Ыr─Бddha on the former, while those who have not kept srauta fires and s┼лdras should offer ┼Ыr─Бddha on the latter,

Sr─Бddhas are divided into three classes, nitya, naimitteka and k─Бnya. An observance is called nitya when it is laid down that it must be performed on a certain or fixed occasion ( such as every day, on an am─Бv─Бsy─Б, or on Astak─Б day). What is laid down for being done on an occasion which is uncertain is celled naimiitika ( such as the birth of a son). What is ordained to be done in case one desires a certain reward or fruit is called h─Бmija (e. g. the performance of a sraddha on Krttik─Б or Rohini by one who desires heaven or progeny ). The five daily yaljas including pitr-yaj├▒a are nitya i, e, they must be per formed without any eye to any reward therefrom and the

[Vol. Very learned disquisitions are held in Apar─Бrka p. 465 ff, Hem─Бdri p. 313 ff and other writers and digests as to the mean ing of apar─Бhna which is the time for sraddha prescribed by Manu (III. 278). The classification of Sraddhas. Sraddhas have been variously classified. One classification, viz, into nutya, nazm─▒ttrica and Lamya has already been desoribed above (p. 369) Another classification is that into Ekoddista and P─Бryana 855. The first is offered to one deceased person alone, while the latter is performed on the am─Бv─Бsy─Б of a montl─▒ or in the dark half of Bhadrapada or on sankr─Бnti and in it the three paternal ancestors are principally invoked. These classifications and enumerations of ┼Ыr─Бddhas will afford an idea how the doctrine of ┼Ыr─Бddhas was carried to an exaggerated extent in the course of centuries. It goes without saying that only a few people could have indulged in the luxury of so many ┼Ыr─Бddhas a year and most people were content with the performance of only one Mah─Бlaya┼Ыr─Бddka and one or two more. It may be noted that Manu (II. 122) first prescribed that on the am─Бv─Бsy─Б of each month an elaborate ┼Ыr─Бddha should be performed, but knowing that this was almost impossible Manu recommends to all (IIL. 281 ) that an elaborate ┼Ыr─Бddha should be performed on three am─Бv─Бsy─Бs in one year 862 (viz. in Hemanta, Grisma and Varsa) and one should perform every day the ┼Ыr─Бddha which is one of the five daily sacrifices (III. 82-83). Devala went further and recommended that an elaborate ┼Ыr─Бddha may be performed only once a year,

Who should be invited at ┼Ыr─Бddha

who has studied the Veda and is able to teach the whole Veda with its angas, a Srotriya-mthese persons sanctify the company if they eat at a funeral repast. Gaut. 15. 28, Baud. Dh. S. II. 8.2, Manu II 185тАУ186, Y─Бj I, 219, Var─Бhapur─Бna 14,2 contain almost the same words about those who sanctify the company of diners (ie who are panktip├╡rana). The Anu┼Ы─Бsanaparya (90.25-31), K┼лrmapur─Бpa II. 21.1-14, Matsya 16 7-13, Brahmapur─Бna 220. 101-104, V─Бyu 79. 56-59 and 83, 52-55, Skanda VI. 217, 21-25 give long lists of panktip─Бvana brahmanas. The Hir. Gr. I. 10.2, Baud, Dh. S. II.2.7, K─Бrma (IT, 21. 14) and others say that & performer of sriddha should invite one who is not a relative connected by marriage (such as & maternal uncle) nor one who is of the same gotra, nor one who is connected with the performer by Veda study (i. e. is his teacher or pupil), nor a friend nor one Tho expects monetary help from the performer. Manu (III. 138-139 ) provides that one should not invite at & ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner & personal friend, that one may gain a friend by making Taluable gifts to him (on other occasions), that one should feed at a br─Бddha & brahmaba whom he does not deem either his friend or foe and that he who performs gr─Бddhas and offer ings to gods chiefly to gain friends reaps no reward after death by those sraddhas or offerings, But Manu IIL 144 (= K┼лrma II 21-22) provides that one may invite even a friend but not a foe though the latter may be learned. Manu (II. 135тАУ137 and 145тАУ147 ) lays down that the main or best rule to be followed is to present ┼Ыr─Бddha food to those who are devoted to spiritual knowledge, that between a man who has studied one whole recension of the Veda but whose father was not a ┼Ыrotriya and one who is himself not a ┼Ыrotriya but whose father had studied a whole recension of the Veda (i.e.whose father was a ┼Ыrotriya) the latter is the more worthy of the two, that one should strive to feed at a sraddha an adherent of the Rgveds who has studied one entire recension of that Veda or a follower of the Yajurveda who has studied ons Sakha thereof or a singer of samans who has finished one recension of the Samaveda and that if one of these preceding three is honoured and dines at a sraddha, the ancestors of the performer will be gratified up to the seventh generation for a very long time. Harita (q. by Hem─Бdri on ┼Ыr─Бddba p. 392 and Kalpataru on ┼Ыr. pp. 66-67) describes the qualifications of those who are pankteya br─Бhmanas viz, they must be born in a high family (possessing four characteri stics), must be endowed with learning (of six kinds) and sila

The Matsyapur─Бpa (16. 11-12) recommends ‘He who expounds (the meaning of) texts; he who enters upod the discussion of srauta sacrifices and he who knows the rules about the accents of s─Бmans is a purifier of panktip─Бvanas; one proficient in the S─Бmaveda, a Vedic student, one endowed with knowledge of the Veda or of Brahma

where these are fed in a fr─Бddha it yields the highest benefit.’ 871 Though in the above passages the greatest emphasis was laid on the possession of Vedic learning by the br─Бhmanas to be fed, one had also to see whether they were men of good character and observers of the rules of proper conduot, as provided by A┼Ыv, Gr. IV. 7, 2 (note 862), Gaut. 15.9 and Manu L. 118 who says ‘a br─Бhmana 872 knowing only the sacred Gayatri but living a well-regulated life is to be preferred and not one who knows the three Vedas but who is not well-regulated in conduct and who eats anything (even forbidden food ) and who is a vendor of everything.’ The Skandapurana VI. 217. 27 recommends that one should make every effort to know the family of the br─Бhmanas, then their character (┼Ыila), then their age and then the facts about whom they marry or to whom they give their daughters in marriage. The Brahm─Бnda (Upodgh─Бta, chap 15) says that there should be no scrutiny of a br─Бhmapa about whom nothing is known because s─▒ddhas (yogins) roam about on the earth in the form of br─Бhmanas. But if faults in a br─Бhmana are easily seen or if one knows his disqualifica tions on account of one’s dwelling near him, he should not be invited (versos 5-6). The same Pur─Бpa (Upodgb─Бta 15. 24-26) arranges the orders of preference as follows: first yati (ascetic), then a br─Бhmana who knows the four Vedas and itib─Бsa, then one who knows three Vedas, then one who knows two, then one who knows one Veda, then one who is an upadhy─Бya. These requirements of learning, character and good conduct would naturally make it incumbent on the performer of a gr─Бddha to inquire into the antecedents, qualities and defects of the br─Бhmanas to be invited, Manu and others lay down Beveral rules about the testing of the brahmapas to be invited. Manu III 149, Viс╣гс╣Зu Dh.874 S. 82.1-%. provide at an offering to the gods let a man not enquire into (the qualities of a brahmana (when he wants to invite), but at a gr─Бddha offering to the Manes Olose inquiry (into qualities) is declared to bB proper and just.’ Madu III, 130 says that even if a brahmana be master of the Veda, one should enquire far (into his ancestry). The Vayupur─Бna 675 appears to provide that inquiry into ( the qualifications of) br─Бhmands should not be always undertaken when gifts are to be made, but enquiry is declared (necessary) in the case of rites for gods and Manes. The Anusa sanaparya provides 876 that in rites meant for gods & ksatriya knowing the rules about gifts should not (closely) inquire into the qualifications of br─Бhmanas, but in rites for the gods and Manes such inquiry is quite proper. Vrddha-Madu and the Matsya-pur─Бna877 lay down that a br─Бhmana’s character is to be inquired into at the place where he resides for a long time, his purity by his acts and transactions with other people, his iptelli gonce by discussion with him; with these three one should inquire whether the br─Бbmapa (to be invited) is a worthy person,

Inquiring into qualifications

391

IV

The Nrsimhapur─Бna. 878 forbids close inquiry into the character and learning of one who comes by chance as a guest at the time of gr─Бddba. That inquiry was allowed as to br─Бhmadas who were invited and not as to those who came by chance uninvited as anthis. There are no doubt certain passages particularly in the Puranas where scrutiny into & br─Бhmana’s qualifications is condemned. For example, the Skandapur─Бna quoted by Apa r─Бrka (p. 455) and Kalpataru ( on ┼Ыr. p. 102) states The Vedic revelation is that ┼Ыr─Бddha is to be offered (to & br─Бhman&) after inquiry (into his learning and character), but straightforward action is better than scrutiny. When one offers sr─Бddha straightforwardly without inquiry his pitrs are gratified and also gods’. The Bhaviс╣гyapur─Бpa (q.. by Balanbbatti) states ‘it is my view also that one should not test (the qualifications of) br─Бhmanas; one should only consider their caste and not their virtues’. Such passages are explained away as referring to a ┼Ыr─Бddha at sacred places or as applicable to gifts or to atthis (vide Hemadri op sraddha p. 513, and Balambhatti on ─Бc─Бra p. 494) 8784,

Brahmanas vere declared to be apankteya 879 (not fit to sit in the row of brahmana diners or as defiling & row of diners at ┼Ыr─Бddha) on various grounds, such as bodily and mental defects and diseases, purauit of certain avocations, moral lapseg, being guilty of crimas, being followers of unorthodox systems, being inhabitants of certain countries. A distinction has to be made batween br─Бhmanas who should not be invited and brahmapas that are ap─Бnkteya or panktid┼лsaka. For example, one should not ordinarily javite a friend or a sagotra br─Бhmana even

Hem─Бdri (Sr─Бddhak─Бnda, pp, 380-385 ) holds an intereste ing disoussion as to whether a performer of ┼Ыr─Бddha belonging to one recension of a Veda must restrict himself to inviting br─Бhmanas that are students of the same recension of the Veda or whether he can invite any br─Бhmana that may bave studied any of the three Vedas. Some people relying on a maxim (‘as in the case of a bride so in the case of an offering’) invite only brahmanas of their own ┼Ы─Бkh─Б possessed of the qualifications above set forth. Hem─Бdri replies tbat this is a wrong notion, relies on Ap. Dh, S. II. 6. 15. 9 ‘one should feed 887 in all (religious) acts br─Бhmapas that are pure (in their conduct) and that have studied the Veda’ and asserts that no smrti, Itihasa, Pur─Бda, Grhyas┼лtra nor Kalpas┼лtra contains the restriction of inviting only br─Бhmadas of the performer’s own ┼Ы─Бkh─Б, He further says that in such texts as ’trip─Бciketas trimadhuh’ (quoted in note 862a above) the rule laid down is to inpite br─Бhmavas that have studied different sakh─Бs and Vedas. He rejects the idea about any restriction as to selecting a bridegroom of the same ┼Ы─Бkh─Б as the bride’s father and remarks that if some people are not prepared to give their daughters in marriage to young men belonging to other ┼Ы─Бkh─Бs, that is due to ignorance about the families and is also due to pride ‘and vanity. He winds up by saying that in Ary─Бyarta countries it is found on all sides that marriage connections are entered into with persons studying different ┼Ы─Бkh─Бs but living in the same district, (such connections) not being con demned, while persons who study the same ┼Ы─Бkh─Б of the Veda but do not know each other do not enter into marital connec tions.888 As a contrast to this commonsepse view it should be

ing (of food) is eaten by a zati that knows the truth about - pralcrti (primordial matter) and the gunas (sattva, rajas and tamas) reaps the reward (merit) of feeding a thousand (other br─Бbmapas), Therefore one should feed in offerings to gods and manes an excellent yogin who is intent on true knowledge of God and others only if such a one is not available. Similar Verses about ascetics and yogins occur in Var─Бhapur─Бna 14, 50, Skanda (VI.217.7ff) and Vayupuranasi chap. 71.65-13, chap. 76.28 &c. Brhaspati provides 892 a special rule that, if a person cannot afford to feed at a ┼Ыr─Бddba more than one brahmana, then he should feed one who has studied the S─Бmaveda, since in him all the three viz. Rks, the Yajus and Samans co-exist, that the father is pljased by Rks (i. e, by the feeding of a brahmana who has studied the Rgveda), the grand-father by Yajus, the great-grand-father by a S─Бman and a chandoga (a chanter of the whole of Samaveda) is superior. A Verse of Satatapa is 893 quoted to the effeot that if a student of the Atharyayeda is fed in a rite for the gods or manes, that yields endless and inex haustible rewards,

Some of the smrtis were very strict in laying down the qualifications of br─Бbmanas to be invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha, Ausa nasa (chap.4) asserts: ’that brahmana 894 is called durbrali mana and should never be invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha in whose family Veda study and Vedi (i. e. the performance of Srauta sacri fices) have been stopped for three generations’. (Vol. author 895 further says that six persons are merely brahma bandhus (i, e. br─Бhmanas by birth or caste alone) viz, one who is hired by a ┼Ы┼лdra or a king as a servant, who has a ┼Ы┼лdra woman as his wife, who is a village priest and he who subsists by killing (animals) or by oatching them. So early as the Mah─Бbh─Бс╣гya 89 it was stated that austerities (leading a life of restraint and strict observances), Vedic learning and birth (from br─Бbmapa parents) are the causes of (a man being called) a br─Бhmada and that he who is devoid of the first two is a mere brahmana by caste (but not a real br─Бhmapa). It is curious to note that Yama stated that, if brahmanas that do not declare (or point out) the auspicious naksatra or tathi or day or mu. harta and other auspicious matters, eat (sraddha) food it be comes inexhaustible.

But the requisite qualifications were so exacting that it must have been found almost impossible to secure for a ┼Ыr─Бddha br─Бhmabas altogether free from any of the blemishes set out above from Manu. Gautama (15 15-18) contains long lists 897 of over 50 kinds of br─Бhmadas that were not to be invited at a ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner or at a sacrifice for gods, but Gaut, adds that according to some only those beginning with “durv─Бla’ (Gaut, in 15.18) were to be shunned at a ┼Ыr─Бddha (but could be invited at a sacrifioe for the gods). [Vol. choice of) ineritorioua br─Бlmanas; thereforo one should not desire a large company 907 The K┼лrorapur─Бpa (uttarardha 22.32 ) insists that an atithe must be fed at a ┼Ыr─Бddha or other, wise the ┼Ыr─Бddha is not praiseworthy. Though these ancient works insisted upon the avoidance of large preparations and expenses for ┼Ыr─Бddhas in honour of a deceased person, there were other smrtis that favoured lavish distribution of wealth in ┼Ыr─Бddhas. For exan─▒ple, Brhaspati lays down: ‘( An heir ) should lay aside half of the wealth that comes to him (by inheritance ) for the benefit of the deceased owner and should expend it in the monthly, six-monthly and yearly ┼Ыr─Бddhas’. The D─Бyabh─Бga XI. 12 approves 908 of this and also quotes Ap, Dh. S. II. G. 13.3 ‘On the failure of a sapinda the teacher of the Veda takes the wealth of the deceased, on failure of the teacher, the pupil takes it and having inheri ted it he should employ it in the performance of works of charity for the benefit of the deceased’ (or he himself may enjoy it). These passages show to what lengths the cult of benefit to the soul of the deceased was carried in India by certain writers. More practical authors such as Haradatts did not relish these extreme views. In severa) pur─Бdas such as the Vayu 9084 and Visou there are express directions that when a ┼Ыr─Бddba is performed at Gay─Б, it should be on a profuse scale and no stinginess 909 (lit. cheating in money matters ) in spending wealth should be shown there; otherwise the performer would not reap the benefit of the performance of ┼Ыr─Бddha at that holy place. expenditure of wealth in all ┼Ыr─Бddhas, The V─Бyupur─Бna 910 (82, 26-28 ) further says that the br─Бhmapas of Gay─Б are super men, that when they are gratified (at a ┼Ыr─Бddha) the gods together with pitrs become gratified, that no question should be raised about the family, the character, the learning and the austerities (of the Gay─Б br─Бhmadas), that by honouring them a man attains liberation, that a man after honouring the br─Бbmanas should proceed according to his resources and strength to the performance of ┼Ыr─Бddha, thereby he secures all heavenly desires and obtains the means of Moksa. The Skanda pur─Бpa goes so far as to say that Gay─Б br─Бbmanas even if they are depraved in their conduct and are backward deserve to be invited at sraddha and are superior to br─Бhmadas who have mastered the Veda and Ved─Бngas. The Nirnayasindhu (IIT. P. 401 ) notes that, according to the Tristhalisetu of his grandfather, this provision holds good only in the case of the ┼Ыr─Бddha at the Aksayya Vata in Gay─Б and nowhere else. In modern times the br─Бhmanas at Gay─Б. used to require the performer of ┼Ыr─Бddha while he was in the sacred Phalgu river to make a declaration about his wealth and demanded fees accordingly, thereby carrying to the letter the words of the V─Бyupur─Бna, Many people returned from Gaya thoroughly dis illusioned and disgusted with the conduct of the br─Бhmanas at Gay─Б. In the Var─Бhapur─Бna 911 it is said that two yerses were sung by the pitrs viz Would such a blessed and intelli gant man be born in our family who will offer piodas (i. e. sr─Бddha) to us without being stingy about wealth and who would bestow on br─Бhmanas with reference to us (i. e. for our benefit) jewels, clothes, land, costly vehicles and all other kinds of wealth including water, when he has riches enough? Mode of inviting a br─Бhmana

brother or a pupil or a br─Бhmaс╣Зa, but it should not be given through a person of another varс╣Зa 916 or a woman or a child or person belonging to another gotra por from a distance (Prajapati 64). Pracetas provides that a br─Бhmaс╣Зa performer of ┼Ыr─Бddha when giving an invitation should touch the right knee, a ksatriya inviter the left knee of the invitee, a Vai┼Ыya inviter should hold both feet of the invitee and a s─Бdra should prostrate himself at the feet of the invitee (vide Sx. History of Dhar ma┼Ы─Бsira

(Vol.

mana who bas been invited (to a ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner) by a faultless performer should not refuse the invitation nor should lie, aftor being invited (and having acoepted the invitation), accept a gift of even (uncooked) food from another person. Manu III 190 and K┼лrmapur─Бna provide that if a brahmada after recairing on invitation for a sacrifice to gods or manes according to s─Бgtra directions and after having accepted at violates the appoint ment, he incurs sin and becomes a hog 921 (in his next birth). This does not apply where he is unable to go on account of illness or other valid reason.

The smrtis laid down some strict and elaborate rules which were to be observed by the br─Бbmapas invited for ┼Ыr─Бddha and by the performer himself. IV:

What milk and water to be used

415

From considerations of space this matter cannot be pursued further. The Mit, on Yaj. I 240 puts together a long list of allowed and of condemned kinds of grains and other articles,

What milk should be ordinarily partaken of and what sliould be avoided has been dealt with in H. of Dh, vol. II pp. 782-783. A few words are added here. Manu III, 271 and Y─Бj.I. 258 provide that if cow’s milk or rice cooked therein (called payasa) is offered in ┼Ыr─Бddha the pitrs are satisfied for one year. V─Бyu 78.17, Brahma 935 220 169, M─Бrkandeya 32 17-19, Vispupur─Бna III.16.11 forbid the use in a ┼Ыr─Бddha of the milk of a she-buffalo, of a camari or female deer, of sheep or eves, of she camels, of human females and of all animals with one hoof and the use of the curds and clarified butter prepared from such milk. But ghee prepared from buffalo milk was allowed by Subantu and Devala (q. by Hem─Бdri on ┼Ыr─Бddha p. 572 ).

The M─Бrkandeyapurana 936 (29.15-17), Vayu (78.16) and Visoupurana (I 16 10) lay down that the water to be employed in sraddha must not have a bad smell, must not be foamy, or taken from a puddle or a small reservoir which cannot slake the thirst of a cow, must not have been brought oveinight, must not be taken from a reservoir not dedicated to all or from a trough or the like meant for beasts.

Several rules are laid down about the fruits, roots and vegetables recommended or condemned for use in sraddha, For example, the Brahma-pur─Бpa (220.156-158 ) enumerates several kinds of fruits such as mangoes, bilza, pomegranate, cocoanut, dates, grapes, as fit to be given in ┼Ыr─Бddba. Vide Saс╣Еkha 14 22-23 also. Tayu (78 11-15 ) states 936r that garlic, leeks and onions, other things that are of bad odour or taste

securing their favour. In course of time that conception grew str. onger and stronger, so much so that Manu (V.27-44 and V.46-47) and Vasistha appear to be in two minds (vide H. of Dh. vol. II pp. 778-780). Gradually the offering of flesh in Madhuparka and in ┼Ыr─Бddhas came to be totally condemned in works of the 12th and 13th centuries and onwards as a matter prohibited in the Kali age (Var─Бtithipitrbhya┼Ыca pas┼лp─Бkaranakriya ). (Vide H. of Dh, vol. III pp. 945-946 and p. 964). Now except among the br─Бhmanas (in Northern India ) who have no objection to include fish in diet as permissible to them no br─Бhmana offers flesh in sraddha, The usage of Northern India would be in accordance with the view set out in Brhann─Бrad─лya pur─Бna that one should offer honey, flesh and other things according to the usage of the country, as explained by the Prthyicandrodaya.

Manu (V.11-18) contains long lists of animals, birds and fishes whose flesh was not to be eaten oven by those who were flesh-eaters,

If a person is destitute, some of the Pur─Бpas such as the Vispu (III. 4.24-30) and the Var─Бha (19,53-58) mercifully provide in identical 955 verses that instead of entertaining br─Бbmanas with a sumptuous dinner or flesh the poor man may offer only un cooked corn, or some vegetables growing wildly or some slight daksin─Б if he cannot offer even uncooked food or vegetables, or he may offer a few grains of sesamum (7 or 8) to a br─Бhmana with water in his folded hands, or grass to a cow enough for one day and if he cannot afford even any one of these, tben he may repair to a thicket of trees, raise his arms so that bis armpits are exposed and loudly address the guardians of the worlds such as the Sun in the following words: ‘I have neither wealth zor money nor anything else it to be offered by way of ┼Ыr─Бddha; I bow to my pitrs; may the pitrs be satisfied by my devotion; I have stretched these arms in spacel’ (lit, the path of the wind).

Malapitrijajna in Sakamedha

formed in Sakamedha, the third of the four Caturm─Бsyas: “He offers to Soma accompanied by the pitrs a cake baked on six potsherds, to the pitrs Barhisadah (sitting on darbha grass or in a yaj├▒a) fried grains, for the pitrs called Agnisv─Бtta he milks a drink from a cow which has to be won over (to another calf). This for thee, O father and for those who come after thee (i. e, for thy descendants); this for thee, O grandfather, great-grandfather and for those who come after thee; do, ye Pitrs rejoice in your portions. May we gladden thee, O Indra, that castest thy glance at us, como forth now with full chariot seat; being praised (by us) thou goest to places desired by you. Yoke, O Indra, thy two bay steeds. They (patarah) bave eaten, they have rejoiced, the dear ones have dispelled (evil); the radiant sages have been praised with newest hymn, Yoke,O Indra, thy two bay steeds. The pitrs have eaten, the pitrs have rejoiced, the pitrs have been glad, the pitrs have purified themselves. Go away, O Pitrs, that art soma-loving by your majestic ancient paths. Then reach ye the mitrs that well know you (or everything) and that revel in the company of Yama.”

[Vol. He says ’to Soma drunk by the pitrs, sradhal Adoration!’ He says ’to Agni, the carrier of kavja, svadh─Бl Adoration ! (Thereby) he pleases the fire that pertains to the pitrs. He offers (into fire) three oblations; he puts down (on the darbhas spread on the ground) three pindas. (These) thus come to six in number. Six indeed are the seasons. He (thereby) pleaseg the seasons The seasons are indeed the shining (or divide) pitrs……The darbha grass is cut with one stroke; the pitrs have as it were (passed away) once for ever. He puts down thrice (the pindas) The pitс╣Ыs are indeed in the third world from here. He (thereby) pleases them. He (the performer) turns his face away (to the north from the south), for the Fathers are shy, He remains with his face turned away till the steam (of the boiled rice of the pindas) ceases to rise, for the Fathers have the steam of rice as their share; he should simply emell (the pipdas). That as if does not amount to eating of non-eating. The pitс╣Ыs when departing (from the ┼Ыr─Бddha rite) take away or grant a valiant son. He cuts off the fringe (of a garment to place it on the pindas), for the share of Fathers is taking away (what is offered). He (thereby) allots their proper share to the pitrs (and dismisses them). When the performer) is in the latter part of life (i e, over 50 years of age) he cuts off hair (from his chest instead of presenting a dasa) At that time he is nearer to the pitrs (when above 50 years of age). He offers adoration, because adoration (namask─Бra) is dear to the pitrs, Adoration to you, O Fathers, for vigour; adoration to you, o fathers, for life, adoration to you, O fathers, for sadha, adoration to you, O fathers, for ardour; adoration, O fathers, for the terri ble! O fathers’ here is adoration to you. This (pindapitryaz├▒a) is indeed a sacrifice of men (i e. sacrifice to departed men) and other sacrifices belong to the gods” In the Tai Br. 1 4 10 the Pitryaj├▒a performed in s─Бkame tha is praised (in 2) and further on it is said that Rtus (seasons) are pitrs and they offered pitryajia to Praj─Бpati, their father. This passage supports the provision made in Manu and some of the digests that the Rtus are to be identified with pitrs and obeisance is to be made to them.%0

IV)

Pindapit ryajsia in sat. Br.

429

The Sat. Br. (II. 4. 2) contains the following somewhat fuller account of the Pjoda-pitryaj├▒a, omitting legendary or other irrelevant matters -When the moon is not seen either in the east or in the west, then he (the performer of the Darsa sacrifice presents food to the Fathers in each month …… He Presents it in the afternoon, The forenoon indeed belongs to the gods; the midday to mon; and the afternoon to the Fathers; therefore le presents (food to the Fathers ) in the afternoon, While seated behind the G─Бrhapatya fire with his face turned towards the south and the sacred thread on his right shoulder be takes that material (for the offering from the cart). There upon he rises from thence and threshes the rice while standing north of the Daksina fire and facing the south. Only once does he clean the rice, for it is once for all that the fathers have passed away. He then boils it. While it stands on (the Daksina fire) he pours some clarified butter on it. After remov ing it (from the fire) he offers to the gods two oblations in the fire …… Here he is engaged in a sacrifice to the Fathers; hence he thereby propitiatos the gods and being permitted by the gods, he presents that food to the Fathers. He offers to both Agni and Soma ,, He offers with the formula “To Agni, the carrier of kavija (what is offered to the Manes), sv─Бhal’, ‘To Soma accompanied by the Fathers, sv─Бhal’ (V─Б; S. 29). He then puts the pot-ladle (meksapa) on the fire, that being in lieu of the Svistakrt. Thereafter he draws (with the spliya, the wooden sword) one line south of the Daksina fire, that being in lieu of the altar. He then lays down a firebrand at the further (south) end of the line. For, were he to present that food to the Fathers without having laid down a firebrand, the Asuras and Raksasas vould certainly tamper with it. … He lays it down with the text whatsoever Asuras roam about being attracted by the svadha (offering to Fathers), assuming various shapes, be they large-bodied or small-bodied, may Agni expel them from this world (Vaj s. II 30)… He then takes the water jar and makes the Fathers wash (their hands) merely saying ‘N, N., wash thyself’ (naming) the sacrificer’s father; ‘N. N. wash thy self (naming the sacrificer’s) grandfather; ‘N.N., wash thyself

(naming) the sacrificer’s great-grandfather. As one would pour out water (for a guest) when he is about to take food, so in this case, Now those (stalls of sacrificial grass) are sovered with one stroke and cut off near the root; the top belongs to the gods, the middle part to men and the root part (of darbhas) to the fathers. Therefore they are cut off near the roots …… Ho spreads them along with the line with their tops towards the south. Thereon he presents (to tlo fathers the three round cakes of rice). He presents thus for the gods they offer thus for men they ladja out; and in the case of the fathers they do in this very way; therefore he presents the cakes to the fathers) thus With ‘N. N., this for theel’ he presents one cake to the sacrificer’s father. Some add ‘for those that come after thee’, but let him not say this, since he himself is’one of those to whom it would be offered in comcuon. Let him therefore merely say ‘N, N., this for thee!’ as to the sacrificer’s father; “N. S. II, 31). Whereby he says ‘Eat each his own share’. He then tuins round to the left so as to face the opposite (north) side; for the fathers are far away from men; and thereby he also is far away (from the fathers), ‘Let him remain (standing with bated breath) until his breath fail’ say some; ‘for thus far extends the vital energy’. However, having remained so far a moment-he again turns round (to the right) and mutters “the Fathers have regaled themselves; like bulls they have come each to his own share’ (V─Бj. S. II. 31); whereby what he says is ’they have eaten each his own share. Thereupon he takes the water jar and makes them wash themselves by pouring water on the pindas), merely saying ‘N. N., wash thyself (naming) the sacrificer’s father; ‘N. N. wash thyself’ (naming) his grandfather; ‘N, N., wash thyself’ (naming) his paterna) great-grandfather. Even as one would pour out (water for a guest). When he has taken his meal, so it is here. He then pulls down the tuck (of the sacrificer’s garment) and performs obeisance. The tuok is sacred to the Fathers; therefore he performs obeisance to them after pulling down the tuck. … Six times he performs obeisance, for there are six seasons and the fathers are the seasons, He mutters ‘Give us houses, O fathers, for the fathers are the rulers of houses; and this is the prayer for blessing at this saorifioial performance, After the

The Hir. Gr. (II. 10-13) is more elaborate than the Ap. Gс╣Ы. and not only sets out at length many of the mantras in ─Аp. M. P. II. 19-20, but adds some more. The Sr─Бddhas┼лtra of K─Бty─Бyada (1-3) sets out the procedure of the monthly sraddha almost in the same way as the Y─Бj├▒avalkyasmrti (which is set out below). It states that in the monthly ┼Ыr─Бddha first come the daiva rites and then the various items ocour as in the Pinda-pitryaj├▒a ‘pindapitryaj├▒a-vad-upac─Бrah’ (first s┼лtra of the 2nd kandik─Б) some details which it contains (and Y─Бj. does not expressly mention) may be set out here. It gives in full the mantras ’tilosi’, ‘y─Б divya’ (both of which occur in Asy, gr.), ‘prthivi to patram’ (which is ─Аp. M. P. II. 20.1). It prescribes that in addition to the Gayatri and the Madhumati Verses the word ‘madhu’ should be repeated thrice. The holy texts to be repeated while the br─Бhmanas are engaged in eating according to K─Бty─Бyana are the G─Бyatr─л (once or thrice), the five R─Бksoghni verses (Rg. IV. 4. 1-5, V─Бj. S. XIII, 9-13, Tai, S. I 2. 14, 1-2), Purusas┼лkta, the Apratiratha hymn (Rg. X. 103, 1-13 = V─Б), S. 17. 33-34, 46 = Tai, S. IV. 6.4 1–4) and others, Tt expressly states that the svadh─Бv─Бcana (Y─Бj. I 244) relates to both paternal and maternal ancestors. Besides the blessing contained in Y─Бj I 246, K─Бty─Бyana provides that the performer is to pray for and the brabmanas are to pronounce two more viz, ‘May the pit╚Ъs be kind (lit not dreadful) to us’ and ‘May our family prosper’. Dr Caland in his learned work ‘Altindi scher Ahnencult’ (pp. 150-152) appears inclined to hold that when a s┼лtrak─Бra has not actually said anything on certain iteins in the ┼Ыr─Бddha ritual, one has no right to anticipate, on the authority of later authors, that those items existed in the times of that s┼лtrak─Бra, I demur to this conclusion, Dr. Caland has attached no weight to the fact that Jaimini (as stated in H. of Dh, vol III p 870) laid down the principle that one may include certain items from another ┼Ы─Бkh─Б. Jaimini’s s┼лtras cannot be supposed to have laid down those propositions for the first time. Jaimini’s s┼лtras are at least as old as some of the extant srauta s┼лtras such as that of K─Бty─Бyana Therefore hardly any chrono logical conclusions can be drawn with certainty from the silence of a s┼лtrak─Бra as to a certain item in the ┼Ыr─Бddha ritual.

It should be noticed how closely the Padmapurana follows the procedura (including the mantras ) contained in Yajna. Yalkya. What procedure the author of a Purana follors depends upon his learning and the s┼лtra that he studied. For example, the Visgudbarmottara 1140 appears to rely on the ─Аp gr. and the Ap. M. P. (IL 19-20), since I 140.12 refers to ─Аp M.P. I. 19.1 , 1. 140, 29-30 to Ap. M. P. I. 19. 14-16, I, 140.35 to ─Аp M P. I 20.1. Similarly, Skapda (VI 224 3-51) closely follows ─А┼Ыv. go and Y─Бj.

Oring to the difference in details of ┼Ыr─Бddha in the several gshyag┼лbras, the smrtis and the pur─Бnas, an important question arises whether a person should perform a ┼Ыr─Бddha rite only in Bocordance with the grhyas┼лtra of his own Veda or Sabh─Б or whether he may perform it after the inclusion (upasainh─Бra) of

  1. gada Matsya 17. 56-57,IV)

The mat─▒m of ‘sarva┼Ыalch├╡pratyaya’

433

the several items found in other s┼лtras and smrtis though not included in the kalpa or grhya s┼лtra of his own S─Бkh─Б, This topic is discussed at great length by Hem─Бdri (on ┼Ыr─Бddha ) pp. 748тАУ759 and briefly by Medh─Бtithi on Manu II, 29 and XI. 216, by the Mit on Y─Бj. IIL 325, Apar─Бrka p. 1053 and others. Those who are for strictly following the details in one’s own sutra alone argue as follows: If one were at liberty to include details other than those contained in one’s own s┼лtra, the order of the details (lama) given in one’s s┼лtra and the time specified for each detail would be interfered with Besides, if the addition of details were permissible, one would be liable to the charge of giving up the usages of one’s own family handed down for generations. These objectors rely upon such passages as that of the Viс╣гс╣Зudharmottara which states ‘He who violating ( the dictates of) his own s┼лtra acts according to & s┼лtra meant for others, treats thereby his own sage ( the author of his s┼лtra) as unauthoritative and incurs ( the blame of doing what is in proper,‘1010 The smrtis that contain additional details may be meant for those men who have no kalpa or grl─▒ya s┼лtra of their own or they may be useful for s┼лdras.

Those who espouse the view that as far as possible all details found in several grhyas┼лtras and smrtis on one rite should be included by every one rely mainly on Jaimini II. 4.8-33 which is called ‘s─Бkhantar─Бdhikarapanyaya’ or ‘sarya┼Ы─Бkh─Бpratyaya nyaya’. The principal sutra is Jai. II, 4. 9.1011 It is established in this s┼лtra that the prayorana (purpose ) or phala (reward to be secured) of the rite is the same in different s┼лtras and smrtis. For example, the rewards of ┼Ыr─Бddha are stated to be the same in all s┼лtras and smrtis (vide notes 787тАУ790 above); then the dravia (materials) and the deity are the same (in P─Бrvana ┼Ыr─Бddha the deities are the paternal ancestors and the materials,

Egnihotra and the like’. 1913 The first verse of K─Бty─Бyana may be explained as applying where one’s ┼Ы─Бkh─Б or s┼лtra deals with a matter without requiring any addition or as the next best course where one is not able to supplement one’s s┼лtra owing

The to some unseen cause or owing to human difficulties. Sangraha says that where different items of the ┼Ыr─Бddha rite are declared to be performed at different times and there is no agreement among the sages, one should follow one’s grhya s┼лtra, but where one’s grhyas┼лtra is silent as to a certain item or as to the stage when it is to be performed, there is an option and one may follow the opinion of some sage as to that item. 1014 It appears that even the ancient grhya s┼лtras exhibit tendencies that led to the sarvasakha-pratyaya-nyaya e. g. Asv. gr. (g. in n 966) employs several passages (such as Tilosi’, ‘Ya. divya,’ which do not occur in the Rgveda.)

It is owing to this maxim of ‘sarva┼Ы─Бkh─Б-pratyayany─Бya’ that medieval digests go on heaping up details from all smrtis and pur─Бnas in their descriptions of the several gr─Бddbas, the procedures of which were not originally very extensive.

(VOL who have shaved themselves and pared their nails, should offer them materials for brushing the teeth and request them to sit down on separate seats, then give them oil and water for bathing. Before proceeding to give some idea as to how the p─Бrvana ┼Ыr─Бddha was dealt with in medieval and modern times, observa tions must be made on several relevant matters, on which there is a difference of views or which are important in a general way.

When the invited br─Бbmapas come after noon, it is pro vided in some of the pur─Бnas that two mandalas should be made in front of the performer’s residence for receiving the br─Бh madas. For example, the N─Бradapur─Бna states 1016 the mandala for a br─Бhmana performer should be square (four cornered) in size, for a ksatriya triangular, circular for ─Б vaisya and for a ┼Ы┼лdra mere sprinkling of the ground with water is enough.’ The mandalas should be made on ground smeared with cowdung and with water mixed with cow’s urine. Of the two mapdalas one should be on the northern side sloping towards the north and the other on the southern side sloping towards the south. On the northern mandala ku┼Ыas with points towards the east should be placed along with aksata (unbroken or whole) grains and on southern one double-folded ku┼Ыas should be placed along with sesamum grains. The northern mandala should generally be two cubits on each side while the southern one should be four cubits on each side. The brahmana or br─Бbmanas that repre sent the Visiedev─Бh should be honoured in the northern mandala first by the performer himself with water for washing their feet after bending his right knee and the br─Бbmapas representing the pitrs should be then honoured in the southern mandala with water for washing the feet (hence called padya) after bending his left knee. The Todar─Бdanda (┼Ыr─Бddba saukuya ) following Manu TII, 282 states that one who is an Agnihotrin cannot perform a p─Бryana-┼Ыr─Бddha on any day except on darsa (i. e, on am─Бv─Бsy─Б).

Another important question on which thero is great diver gence concerns the number of abutis to be offered in agnau harana, the deities to whom the loma was to be offered, the order in which the deities were to be named and the form of words to be used. On those matters there appears to have been divergent views from very ancient times. According to the Sat, Br. II. 4. 2. 12-13 the ─Бhutis were only 1027 two, they were offered to Agni and Soma in that order and the word sv─Бh─Б was used at the end. According to the Tai. Br I 3. 10.2-3 2028 the khutis were three, they were to be offered to Soma, Agni and to Yamna in that order and the formula ended with ‘syadha namah (and not with ‘sv─Бh─Б ‘). Various rules of etiquette about serving food, about the way brahmapas are to eat and related matters have been laid down from ancient times and are observed even now. The Sm, C (p.465-470), Hemadri (raddha pp. 1367-1384), the Sr. Pr. pp. 116-123 and other digests contain elaborate rules on these

matters. Yaj.I. 237 prescribes that what remains after offering homa should be served in the plates meant for the brahmanas representing the Fathers and the plates should preferably be

IV)

Rules about serving food. side dishes viz. brotl─▒s, vegetables, milk, curds, gheo and honey on the ground (and not on a wooden stool or the like ). The vessels placed on the ground should contain various kinds of food (such as sweetmeats, p─Бyasa), fruits and roots, delicious flesh, spiced or perfumed drinks. Having brought near the brahmanas all the vessels containing food, he should serve it in the plates declaring the characteristic of each kind of food (saying this is sweet, this is sour’ &c.). The performer wliile serying should not shed tears (remembering his ancestors ), be should not become angry, should not utter falsehood, he should not touch the (vessel containing) food with his foot and should not serve food with a violent jerk, Whatever is liked by the br─Бhmanas should be served to them without any grumbling and he should talk about Brahma ( or about Vedic riddles ), because that is agreeable to the pitrs. The perfornier himself, being pleased, should ( by his sweet speech ) gladden the br─Бhmadas, should make them partake of food without Jiurty, and should urge them on frequently (to take more food) by declaring the good points of the various items of food. All food should be steaming hot and the br─Бhmanas should partake of it silently and should not themselves speak of the good points of the food even when questioned by the performer. When the food is hot, when the br─Бhmanas eat in silence and when the good qualities of the food are not declared by the br─Бhmanas, the Fathers partake of it. When a br─Бhmana (at a ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner) partakes of food, having his head covered with a garment (& turban &c)or facing the south or having his sandals on, evil spirits partake of the food (and not the Fathers).’ As early as Gaut., it is provided that the food for the braumapas should be of the highest sort and should be enriched by condiments and flavoured,

Some of the other rules are : The Praj─Бpati-smrti (verses 57-62) states who should cook the food for the ┼Ыr─Бddha dinner. The wife, any fortunate (or handsome) woman of the performer’s gotra whose husband is living and who has a son or brother and is devoted to waiting upon her elders, the performer’s teacher’s wife, his maternal uncle’s wife, paternal or maternal aunt, bis sister, his daughter or daughter-in-law, all of them having their husbands alive, should engage in the cooking of the food for ┼Ыr─Бddha. Women of good family, who have a large progeny, whose husbands are alive and who are about 50 years old or these women if they have become widows, and the wife of one’s paternal uncle or brother, one’s mothers (natural or

each plate for those br─Бhmanas after repeating the mantra ’the earth is thy vessel, the sky is the cover, I offer nectar in the brahmana’s nectar-like mouth; sv─Бha’. Then the performer plunges the (right) thumb of the pitrya br─Бhmana in the food ( the remains of the homa in fire) with the rk or yajus addressed to Viс╣гс╣Зu; and after scattering sesamum grains all round the place where the dinner is to go on with the mantra * the asuras and r─Бkgasas) are struck and driven away he (the performer ) should serve hot food very much liked (by the departed or by the brahmanas )”. Yaj. I. 238 briefly refers (as translated above) to the mantras and the item of plunging the thumb of the brahmanas in the food; and so does the Baud. Dh. S. also (II. 8. 15-16). The Kalika-purana. prescribes1037 that the thumb of the br─Бhmana should be moved about in the food covered with ghee and honey with the mantra “the earth is thy vessel &c.’ because Viс╣гс╣Зu in the form of the thumb protects food meant for sacrifices to gods and nanes. Saс╣Еkha-Likhita provide 1039 that br─Бhmanas (eating ┼Ыr─Бddba food ) should not declare the good or bad points of the food served, should not say what is untrue, should not praise each other, nor should they say there is plenty of food and drink (and so do not serve more food),

The Matsyapur─лna and some other works provide that the br─Бlmanas should pronounce blessings on the performer (who faces the east) after they have sipped water and have been given water, flowers and akс╣гata grains. The performer prays ‘May our Tatliers be not terrible (i, o, be kind) to us.’ The br─Бbmapas reply “lot it be so’. The performer prays “May our family grow’, ‘May donors increase in our family and also food’, ‘May these blessings turn out to be true’. To all these the br─Бhmanas reply after each one of the prayers 1010 May it be so’. There aro rules about the time when the leavings or particles of food in the plates of the br─Бlmadas that ate the dinner should be removed or swept away Vas. Manu III, 265 (which is the same as Matsya 17 56 and Padma, Srstikhanda 9.185) provides another rule that the leavings of the food in the plates may remain where they are till the br─Бhmanas are dismissed and depart,

Rules about removal of leavings

469

Hem─Бdri (┼Ыr─Бddha, p. 1512 )1041 therefore provides that if the per former has another house the leavings may not be removed till sunset, but if he has only one house, they may be removed after the br─Бhmadas have gone away (vide Yaz I. 257, Matsya 17.56 ). It is further provided by Brhaspati 1042 that the plates should not be removed before the br─Бhmanas Pronounce the word ‘svasti’, and J─Бt┼лkarnya 1043 and the Skandapur─Бna say that the plates and the leavings should be removed by the performer himself or by his pupil or son, but not by women nor by a child nor by one who is not of the same caste Manu III 258 provides that, after the br─Бhmanas have left, the performer should look at the south and pray to the pitrs for certain blessings contained in Manu II 259 which are the same as Y─Бj I 246 translated above (vide p. 447), Vispu Dh, S 73. 28, Matsya 16. 49-50, The Ap. gr. 209 (q. in note 981), ─Аp Dh. S II 7. 17. 16, Manu II, 264, Y─Бj. I, 249 provide that the performer should partake of the remainder of the food cooked for the ┼Ыr─Бddha along with his wife, paternal and maternal relatives after recit ing (according to Haradatta) the Y─Бjusa mantra (Ap. M, P, IT. 20.26 ) which means ’entering the life breath I offer nectar; my soul is centred in Brahman for the sake of immortality. The ─Аp. gr and ─Аp. Dh. 8. provide 1044 that the performer must eat at least a morsel of the food left after serving to the br─Бhmanas. Vy─Бsa and Devala prescribe that on the day of ┼Ыr─Бddha the per former must not observe a fast (even if he usually does so as on Ek─Бda┼Ы─л or ┼Ъivar─Бtra). Brahm─Бndapur─Бna 1019 emphatically asserts that this is the correct position as stated by Brhaspati. The Viс╣гс╣Зu Dh. S. (73 15-24) provides that the pindas are to be offered to the ancestors while the br─Бhmanas are actually eating. A fourth view is that of the Ap. gr.24.9, Hir gr. (II. 12.2-3) which state that the per former1050 should, after the brahmanas have eaten and gone away and he has followed and circumambulated them, offer pindas, Owing to this conflict of views Hem─Бdri (quoting smrti) and the Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p 600) say that each one should follow the procedure laid down in his own ┼Ы─Бkh─Б 1051 Hem─Бdri adds that those in whose grhyas┼лtra no special time is mentioned for pindad─Бna should follow the view that pindas are to be offered after the br─Бhmanas have partaken of the dinner and sipped water. There is another conflict of views as regards the ancestors to whom pindas are to be offered at the ┼Ыr─Бddha on am─Бv─Бsya. - Most of the ancient Vedic works refer only to the three paternal ancestors as the devat─Бs of the P─Бrvada-┼Ыr─Бddha and not to any other relatives. The three paternal ancestors are separately the devat─Бs of ┼Ыr─Бddha and 20cumulatively, as indicated by the A┼Ыv, Srauta I, 6.15 and Visu Dh S, 73 13-14, The important questions are whether the vives of the paternal ancestors, viz, the mother, the grandmother and the paternal great-grandmother were associated with their husbands in ancient times and secondly, whether the three paternal ancestors of one’s mother viz. the maternal grandfather, the maternal great-grandfather and the maternal great-great-grandfather were invoked together with their wives in the P─Бrvada The answer to both these questions so far as the Vedas and Br─Бhmanas are concerned is in the negative, Vide Tai, S.1.8. 5.1, Tai.
